GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))

# Analysis

## Ground Truth (GT)
The GT is: `-0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A)`

This contains two basis functions:
1. **A²** (polynomial term)
2. **sin(√A)** (sinusoidal with square root argument)

The key feature is `sin(√A)` — a sine function with `√A` as its argument. This is a very specific transcendental function.

## Candidate Analysis

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(√A)` or equivalent basis functions.

### Candidates with sin():
- **Candidate 4**: `A^c0 * c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5` — has `sin(A*c3 + c4)`, which is `sin` of a **linear** function of A, not `sin(√A)`. These are fundamentally different functions. **No match.**

- **Candidate 6**: `c0 + c1*exp(A*c2) + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5)` — same issue, `sin(linear in A)` ≠ `sin(√A)`. **No match.**

- **Candidate 12**: `c0 + c1*exp(A*c2) + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6*t/(c7*t + c8) + c9/(c7*t + c8)` — same sin issue, plus t-dependence (can zero out t terms, but sin still wrong). **No match.**

- **Candidate 15**: `... + c5*sin(A*c6 + c7) + ...` — sin of linear A. **No match.**

- **Candidate 46**: `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + A^c3*c4 + c5` — no sin at all. This is a sum of power functions. Cannot produce `sin(√A)`. **No match.**

- **Candidate 59**: `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6` — has `A^c1` (could set c1=2 for A²) and `sin(A*c4 + c5)`. But `sin(A*c4 + c5)` ≠ `sin(√A)` since the argument is linear in A, not √A. **No match.**

- **Candidate 61**: `... + A*c3*sin(A*c4 + c5)/(A*c1 + c2) + c6*sin(A*c4 + c5)/(A*c1 + c2) + ...` — sin of linear A. **No match.**

### Candidates with only rational functions and exp():
All remaining candidates (1-3, 5, 7-11, 13-14, 16-45, 47-58, 60, 62-85) are combinations of:
- Rational functions of A (polynomials divided by linear expressions)
- Exponential functions `exp(A*c)`
- Logarithmic functions `log(A*c + 1)`
- Powers of t

None of these can produce `sin(√A)`. The function `sin(√A)` is a transcendental function that cannot be expressed as any finite combination of rational functions, exponentials, or logarithms. These are linearly independent basis function families.

### Key conclusion:
The GT requires `sin(√A)` as a basis function. No candidate contains `sin(√A)` or any equivalent representation. The candidates with `sin()` all have `sin(linear function of A)`, which is fundamentally different from `sin(√A)`.

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), none of these candidates can match the GT.

[NO MATCH]

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT: -0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A)**

The GT contains two basis functions: **A²** (polynomial) and **sin(√A)** (transcendental with √A argument).

Key observation: sin(√A) is a very specific transcendental function. No combination of exponentials, rational functions, logarithms, or sin(linear in A) can exactly reproduce sin(√A) for all A ≥ 0.

Let me categorize the candidates:

**Candidates with sin(A*c + c) terms (Candidates 4, 6, 12, 15, 59, 61):**
These contain sin(c*A + c), which is sin of a LINEAR function of A. The GT has sin(√A), which is sin of √A. Since √A is not a linear function of A, sin(c*A + c) ≠ sin(√A) for any constants. **NO MATCH** for all of these.

**Candidates with only rational functions and exponentials (most candidates):**
These are combinations of rational functions (polynomials divided by linear terms) and exponential terms like exp(c*A). The GT requires sin(√A), which cannot be expressed as any finite combination of rational functions and exponentials. These are all **NO MATCH**.

Let me verify specific candidates:

- **Candidate 4**: A^c0*c1 + c2*sin(A*c3+c4) + c5. Has A^c0 (could match A²) and sin(A*c3+c4) (linear argument, not √A). **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 46**: A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + A^c3*c4 + c5. Pure power law terms, no sin. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 59**: A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3*sin(A*c4+c5) + c6. Has A^c1 (could be A²) but sin(A*c4+c5) has linear argument. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 13, 63**: These have t-dependence through exp(c*t) terms. Setting coefficients to zero would eliminate the A-dependent terms too, making it impossible to match. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 62, 67**: These have A^c5*c6 terms plus rational/exponential. The A^c power could match A², but we still need sin(√A) which isn't available. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 70, 75, 76, 80**: These have t-dependent terms. Setting t-coefficients to 0 leaves rational+exponential in A only. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 12**: c0 + c1*exp(A*c2) + c3*sin(A*c4+c5) + c6*t/(c7*t+c8) + c9/(c7*t+c8). Even zeroing t terms, left with exp and sin(linear A). **NO MATCH**.

After systematic analysis, **none** of the candidates contain sin(√A) or any equivalent representation. All candidates use either:
1. Rational functions of A
2. Exponentials exp(c*A)  
3. sin(c*A + c) (linear argument)
4. log terms
5. Power terms A^c

None of these can produce sin(√A).
